<Author>ladyoblada
<Content>Great Value I stayed at the Aqua Waikiki Wave for two weeks in December '08. I had never been to Hawaii before, so wasn't sure what to expect - I was pleasantly surprised! For the amount of money I paid, I feel I received excellent value: the hotel was in a great location (just a block from prime beach area, near the Int.l Marketplace and Royal Hawaiian Mall); had clean, comfortable rooms that included a DVD player, microwave and fridge; and the staff was always ready to cater to my needs. I also have to rave about the complimentary toiletries: they smelled SO good (a tropical coconut/mango mix)! No bed bugs or strange smells were encountered, as other reviewers noted. But I will admit that noise was a problem...The hotel is next to several night clubs that are active most nights. Ladies of the Night also frequent Kuhio Avenue, as do drug dealers and other shady individuals. They usually come out after 11:00pm. Most nights, the action I witnessed sitting on my lanai was more interesting than anything on television. There are earplugs available in the room for light sleepers though. And there is a STRONG police presence. I generally felt safe, but I wouldn't recommend this hotel as a top choice for families. Some reviewers mentioned a free breakfast...I was never offered one (booked via Expedia), nor was there any information in my room as to where it was located. There was free wireless internet though. The signal was easy to pick up, but it was rather slow at times. Almost as slow as the elevators. But having said that, I would stay here again. It was a good base for a first-time visit to the islands.

<Content>50/50 toss up This hotel ended up being a toss up for us. Some parts we loved other parts not so much. At first the maintenance man tried to argue that we couldn't prove that it was him but after another maintenance man joined us they agreed that they had made a mistake by not covering the car or having us called in the room to move it. It was a slight stress considering that it had us running behind on time to a scheduled tour. The next morning the manager met with us and stated that the car had been detailed and that if there was any issue with the rental car when we returned it to have them call and the hotel would take care of any problems. They also comped the three days of parking that we had. Overall it was a decent stay however we might look for somewhere else next time before staying again.One good thing to remember is that the International Market place is right next to and behind the hotel so it is very convenient to all of the shops and extremely convenient to the beach which is only about a block away

From the bellman, front desk, concierge, to the maids who kept our room clean and neat, they were all just so pleasant and helpful. They were quick to respond to our needs and gave great suggestions for local places to eat and shop. I believe I got an awful lot for the value of the room rate. We paid $195.94 per night including taxes. We had two queen beds, a desk and chair, refrigerator, coffee pot and microwave. There was a continental breakfast offered but we never did check that out. I was very pleased with the service of this hotel. They genuinely wanted you stay to be the best it could and they all did everything they could to make you feel welcomed.SincerelyA Very Satified Customer

<Author>lsnelson
<Content>Wonderful Wave My husband and I just got back from our stay in Waikiki!! We were there for 5 days/4 nights for our good friend's wedding. We are a young married couple without children. We decided to stay at the Waikiki Wave because it was considerably cheaper than the beachfront hotels. Boy am I glad we stayed at the Wave!! Our room was large (2 queen beds for 2 people) and included a good sized mini-fridge, microwave, and coffee pot. From our balcony we could see the ocean to our left, the mountains to our right, and the hustle and bustle of Duke's Alley below. We felt like we were right in the middle of everything- shopping, restaurants, locals, surfers, tourists, etc. The staff was very accomodating and helpful with all kinds of questions and requests, including bus information, information about local beaches, the USS Arizona, etc. The walk to the beach was no longer than 5 minutes and it included many different adventurous routes- through the International Market or the International Food Court- which were both really fun. We also booked a couples massage at the Aqua Bamboo just down the street and it was heavenly and very reasonably priced. We did not go to the pool because we live in the Midwest and preferred to spend our time out in the beautiful ocean. My only complaint pertains to the continental breakfast. It is very minimal (rolls and fruit) but the hotel is right next to several inexpensive restaurants including The Seaside Grill which offers a $3.99 breakfast and also the Food Pantry, a cute little grocery store with a coffee shop and cream puff store attached. (The cream puffs are to die for...) There is also a Denny's and a McDonald's within a block from the Wave. All of the other great things about the Wave definitely made up for the (in my opinion) sub-par breakfast. We were thrilled with our experience at the Waikiki Wave and I wish we were still there! 5 stars to the Wave and mahalo to all of the wonderful cousins!!p.s. I hope to post pictures after a nap today!

<Author>bharrier
<Content>Waikiki Wave - Great Location and Value My wife and I stayed at Waikiki Wave for 8 nights, 8/28-9/5 2008 for our first visit to Hawaii. I made the selection due to the high rating on TripAdvisor as well as the central location. We arrived around 10pm after a 12+ hour flight from Florida via Atlanta...and check-in was quick. I had booked a Deluxe Room...and noticed that the day before we left that although the rate for the first 3 days of our stay had gone up, the last 5 days the cost had gone down...I emailed and asked if we could take advantage of the new rates, and got an immediate email response that canceled our first reservation and a new reservation made that saved us over $100 for the 8 nights. MUCH APPRECIATED!Although we came back many afternoons to find that our room had not been refreshed yet, having previously had part ownership in a Sleep Inn, I can understand the need to make over the rooms of those that check-out before doing the rooms of the continuing guests. Our room was on the 12th floor (1213) which allowed great views to the east -- and even the top most point of Diamond Head, a couple wide views of the Pacific to the south, and view of the north with great rainbows after the short afternoon rain over the mountain. The balcony overlooked the entertainment area of the International Market Place... which always ended by 10pm, so was not an interference at all for sleep.The Expedia staff at the Concierge staff were very helpful in making suggestions for tours, and we did a last minute choice to fly to the Big Island for the Volcano Night tour. We did not rent a car -- but walked almost everywhere due to the central location to Waikiki. We did get the 4-day Visitor Bus Pass for $20 and used it for such trips to Diamond Head and even to the North Shore to get one of the famous snow cones. We had gone past it on our Grand Island Tour a few days earlier ... and Honolulu has an amazing public bus transit system.We usually ate breakfast in our room (did not opt for the continental breakfast plan) since we had a microwave and refrigerator. We found that most all the nicer eating places had lunch prices or early birds until 5 or 6pm. We saved a great deal by eating earlier. This included Cheesecake Factory, Atlantis, etc. The gift shop at the front entrance had deals as good as the International Market Place and Dukes Lane, and went in there about everyday to pick up shirts, hats, even snacks. The clerk was tireless there from open to close and very helpful. (The Food Pantry just a couple blocks away across the street to the east is a full grocery store, and a better option to the ABC Stores for food items - has deli areas as well.)Aqua Resorts seem to have their act together and have done almost a phenomenal job at remodeling this older hotel (a few cracked tiles in the shower, but all plumbing worked fine). The bed was one of the most comfortable we have had in a hotel ... the decor was exactly like their website photos - no bait switch and tactics with the photos. The lobby was smaller than the larger hotels but more than adequate with a seating area, the concierge desks, and a few small shops, plus a couple restaurants, business center, etc. The free Wi-Fi seemed slow although I had a very good to excellent signal ... so opted for my Sprint Broadband Wireless modem most of the time. All the staff from the front desk to maintenance to housekeeping always greeted us with an Aloha and/or Mahalo which shows they really care about their guests.This is certainly a location to consider as an option to the higher priced rooms in the area...and very centrally located.

<Author>lasvegasdude
<Content>Great Value, Great Location, Spotless We were very pleased with our stay at the Aqua Waikiki Wave. The hotel was spotless. Our very large room (jr. suite) was on the corner of the hotel. We had two balconies which proved great for drying beach towels. The staff were very nice and friendly. We spent 9 nights at the hotel and because of the size of the room we never felt cramped. The bathroom is quite small, however. We had in room coffee pot, microwave, ,fridge in the room. Parking is limited on site, but when it fills up parking is available less than a block away. We were charged $18 each day for parking and never really struggled to find a place to park. The hotel is in a very urban environment and Kuhio is a main avenue with plenty of traffic. The noise you'll hear primarliy comes from The Bus and motorcycles. The hotel does provide ear plugs. Something beyond their control was garbage collection each moring about 6:15 AM Mon-Sat. This woke us up each morning but we quickly went back to sleep. We did a lot of walking in the neighborhood with our two sons (ages 7  9). We felt very safe everywhere we went. We were not bothered by anyone. The area was remarkably clean for an urban downtown area. No trash anywhere. The continental breakfast is very limited. In the area there are a vast amount of choices for food. We particularly liked the traditional Hawaiian BBQ drive-in's such as LL, Zippy's, Bob's BBQ, and Rainbow. Delicious food at very affordable prices. $20-30 for lunch or dinner for 4 people. Overall our trip was wonderful. We toured the entire island from the North Shore to the windward coast and everything in between. The hotel added much to our enjoyment of our trip as it surpassed our expectations, from size of the room, condition of the rooms and public areas and the staff.

We had advised the hotel staff of our experience our complaint was not actioned during our stay. No feedback was given to us and no action was taken.  Aside from this, our suite was on the fifth floor facing the International Marketplace and garbage area which disturbingly surrounded the swimming pool. No surprise really that during our week long stay we saw no one swim in the pool - to acces this facility you had to walk past a car park via an alley way climb a flight of stairs to reach the pool which from our fifth floor vantage point we saw was surrounded by garbage bins from nearby food hall.It is disappointing that this recently refurbished property has no double glazing to cut out the noise from the nightly concerts and daily dawn garbage pick-ups. Ear plugs can't drown out the noise and during our stay we were highly inconvenienced by the nocturnal painting on the corridors and doors, fire drills as well as the elevator maintenance during this peak period. There is also very little hot water after 9 p.m.  We are planning another vacation in November back to Honolulu and have decided we will not be staying at this property. We no longer recommend this hotel to our family, friends and colleagues as our stay was marred by these daily incidents compounded by front line staffs lack of concern for guest satisfaction.

<Author>goldboar
<Content>Nice Hotel My girls under 19 soccer team were selected to play in the AYSO National Games in Waipio, HI, this meant that we had to find a hotel that could accommodate a group of 17 girls and parents. After our travel agent delayed our booking at another hotel I found the Wave on Trip Advisor and suggested that we stay there. The reviews on TA were very helpful and right on. This hotel, while not the Marriott is a nice property. The rooms were clean and up to date. Newer carpet, flat screen TVs, microwaves, refrigerators and coffee makers were nice amenities for the rooms. The beds were very comfortable. We stayed in the deluxe rooms on the 11th floor. The hotel staff was very accommodating and arranged for the 5 rooms that we had to be next to each other. Complementary continental breakfast is also included. The sales manager, Evelyn was very accommodating and arranged for the breakfast to open an hour early on the two days that we had early games. The hotel is nicely located about 2 blocks from Waikiki beach front, an easy walk. Also located close to restaurants and shopping.There were only two downfalls of the hotel, the pool was very small and looked like it was an afterthought. It didn't even feel like it was part of the hotel; no spa. Also the parking was very limited, if you weren't in the parking by 6 or 7 pm you had to park an a public parking structure. Make sure you find out from the Wave which structure to park in, the difference can mean paying $6 for 10 hours or $36. The good side was that as long as you provided receipts for other parking you were not changed the $18 parking fee at the hotel.Overall the hotel was a good buy.

The location of the hotel is excellent - smack dab in the middle of Waikiki, surrounded by lots of restaurants and shopping. The beach is less than a 5 minute walk. The street walkers at night are not a problem as neither my husband nor his friend were approached at all and we were with children who were totally oblivious.It does get noisy at night, but you are in Waikiki and you will hear the noise in most hotels anyway. Plus this hotel provides earplugs if you need them.I can't say enough about this hotel, it's location and wonderful staff. We will definitely be staying there again on our trip next year. This hotel, rated 8 of 87 hotels in Waikiki at the time of this review, is a diamond in the rough.....you won't be sorry if you stay, but please remember when comparing hotels to compare apples to apples. <Author>kahuna1959
<Content>Great value, awesome location. My family stayed at the Wave for four nights, 2 in June and 2 in July. We had to make our flight connections in Honolulu for our trip to the big island and Kauai so we added an extra night each way to enjoy Oahu. Overall it was a great deal and the location is fantastic, right next to the international marketplace, about one to two blocks from the beach depending on the route you take. We spent our time on Oahu exploring the shoreline from Diamond head to the north shore and spent very little time in Waikiki.Rooms are quite good. We stayed in a family suite with lots of room and three double beds (one in a room that can be seperated with sliding screens). The beds and bedding are excellent quality. There was a small fridge to keep your drinks cool. Each room had it's own flat screen tv. Yes, the lights in the bathroom are energy savers and take a minute to warm up to full brightness. Leave the lights on if it bothers you and you don't care about saving energy. The hotel is an older building but I think they've done a great job in upgrading the property. The washroom and showers are basic, no high end fixtures but plenty of water and water pressure. Please note if you open a balcony door the air conditioning turns off automatically. We didn't quite close the door all the way and the room warmed up very quickly.Wifi was free and much appreciated. The pool is small, difficult to get to through the parking lot, located in an alley, and your view is a fence. We didn't bother even trying to use it. Parking is tight but we always found a spot.Noise. We were on the 9th and 10th floors during our stay. I had read the reviews and was expecting it to be noisy. I only noticed the noise one night when someone was having a fight/screaming match in the alley below. I have to say it was so noisy that I thought the window had been left open, but it was closed and I could still hear them arguing from the 9th floor. I think it depends on where the noise is coming from and how it bounces off the buildings.Service was excellent with a few qualifiers. I had the same desk person as was noted in some previous reviews. He was attentive and pleasant but neglected to give us some very important information. We didn't know about the continental breakfast on the first floor until our second stay, and we found out about it from another visitor. When we tried to use it the last morning of our stay, we found out you also had to book the breakfast and get vouchers from the front desk, or you had to pay $5 each. For coffee, muffins and some fruit it didn't seem worth $5. It's a very basic continental breakfast but a good deal for free!. It would have been nice to be told about it at check in. We were not told where the pool was. If I hadn't read some reviews before we left I would not have known it was there. We were not told about the overflow parking area but it never came up because we always found a spot. They REALLY need to put a sign up to show the parking lot entrance. We found it on our second time around the block only because the alley seemed the only possible entrance.Brian (or the Big Brown Guy) at the front door was fantastic, really helpful, cheerful and full of Aloha spirit. I hope the management appreciates how much the guests enjoy him.Overall I'd reccomend this place for the price and location. I'd stay here again. Ask for the highest floor possible to reduce the noise.

<Author>thewordgirl
<Content>It made our vacation! We were in Hawaii for what was to be a week of fun and relaxation, and we were supposed to stay with someone we knew who has a condo in Waikiki. It worked out very badly, so we were in need of a hotel QUICKLY, and the Aqua Waikiki Wave was the only one that had a room that wasn't twin beds. We booked and got to the hotel and were greeted by the bellman, who carried ALL of our very HEAVY bags into the hotel for us with a sweet smile on his face. The check in was fast and George and Susan at the front desk were professional and very friendly. We got one of the last rooms that slept three (we had three in our party), and it was a handicapped equipped room. I did not like the bathroom, as it had no shelves (for wheelchair access) or counters, which led to a small mishap in the bathroom. When I called the front desk to complain, I was referred to the manager and told that as soon as they had a free room the next morning, our room would be changed. Imagine my delight when we went out to breakfast only to return later and find that not only had our room been changed, but we'd been upgraded to a suite with two balconies (windows on TWO walls with a view of the mountains!) and a KING and QUEEN bed inside it. Both the standard and the upgraded rooms were equipped with extra electrical outlets, refrigerator, coffee maker and microwave oven. It had an iron and ironing board and a blow dryer (a real one, not one of those wall mounted ones). The rooms are decorated exquisitely, and the color scheme is perfect for the islands. It was such a real delight to find such fantastic and responsive employees and management at this hotel. I will search for the Aqua brand WHEREVER I travel; and I travel a lot.The only cons were the fact that the business center was not gratis, you had to pay 15 cents/minute for internet usage, although wifi in the rooms was provided, and it was very easy to connect and fast. Also, the pool is really small and old because the hotel has been remodeled, (fantastic remodel) but the pool has not yet been done.

I will say the hotel breakfast changes each day, and is sometimes good, and sometimes not, but a Galaxy breakfast will eliminate the need for a big lunch. To the left leaving the hotel is an alley, which is full of street venders, where great deals are to be had,. and if you continue to the beach stay to the right of the Royal hawian hotel(pink) and you will go through the lobby of the Waikiki Sheridan, and come out @ their pool, which if you do @ sunset you will happen up on the nightly hula show. The hotel boosts a very extensive upgrading, indeed the room was newly done, with a very good AC ( shuts itself when you open door to the balcony, nice idea ) with a very nice reprint of Charles W Bartlett art work, excellent bed, lots of pillows, good Oah'u coffee (and Lipton tea bags.) Room was very clean. Room has a refrigerator, a microwave, ironing board and uses good quality shampoo and cream rinse.Nice towels, no bath-robe.The bathroom is still from the 1960's, the ventilation does not work and the room is very very small with ceiling tiles and sink left as is. The counter has been replaced and maybe the tiles around the tub. The shower head is the original one and the draining takes a long time. The commode has a mind of its own and flushes when it feels like it. We visited another room hoping to get a bigger bathroom, to no avail, they are all alike.Honolulu has hundred of hotels, take your time, check around, for $144 per night + taxes, the Aqua Wave is not up to snuff.The housekeeping staff was friendly and responded quickly to exchanging the non-working hair-dryer and the housekeeper on our floor (top floor by the way) always greeted us in the morning. There are apples on the reception desk and the Honolulu advertiser paper is at your door every morning. The hotel is 2 blocks from Waikiki beach and very easy access to bus stops.If you rent a car, the parking is $18 per day, in and out privileges.The location of the hotel is excellent for discovering Honolulu.If we go back we will investigate a different hotel. We faced the International Market and had a double balcony with a nice view of the Royal Hawaiian Hotel and Waikiki Beach in the background. We did hear noise from traffic below, as stated in other reviews, but it did not bother either of us at all. The pool was very small and in the back but we never used it. The location is close to everything. We had rented a car and never had a problem with parking at the hotel.The only complaints we can think of would be the t.v. signal was not that good in our room - but we didn't even notify anyone about it since we hardly watched any t.v. at all; and the flourescent light in the bathroom took a few minutes to get bright. Being that we weren't looking for a luxury hotel, and didn't want to pay right on the beach prices, we were very happy with the Wave. Everyone working at the hotel had lots of Aloha and made us feel comfortable. We would definitely stay at the Wave again! Mahalo.

<Author>gotsit
<Content>Great Value for the Price Just returned today from a 1 week stay with my Mother and Sister to visit family on the island. The biggest reason we chose this hotel was the fact that it had large rooms available with 3 queen beds and had extremely reasonable rates (we got an awesome deal through expedia and paid around $920 per person which included fight, hotel, and taxes). The staff was wonderful and the property was above average. I stayed in room 604 which is sits above the corner of Dukes Lane and Kuhio Blvd. I have to agree with what others had posted about this hotel that it is very noisy due to its location. The first night I stayed there I was awakened by a fight occurring outside one of the bars a little after 4. I'm an extremely heavy sleeper and live in a city so I can pretty much sleep through anything. The problem is that the doors to the lanai's seen to be older and are as noise resistant as newer ones would be. The queen deluxe sweet I was in actually had a separate little bedroom with a sliding wooden door which was pretty neat. This was by far the noisiest part of the room though. The window in that portion of the room was extremely old and would not close properly so at night it was as if the window was wide open and you could hear everything. The bathroom was a little small but was sufficient. A little hint about the lighting in the bathroom. When you first turn the lights on in the bathroom the lighting is extremely dim. You have to let the lights warm up and brighten. We just didn't turn the bathroom light off so it just stayed bright. That is about all the negatives I have. The hotel beds in my opinion were pretty comfortable. The room was huge with a mini-fridge and microwave. There were two LCD TV's in the room neither of which we really used. The decor was very nice as well. The hotel is in a good spot. It is less than a 10 minute walk to Waikiki Beach and all of the shopping. The Ala Moana Shopping Mall shuttle stop across the street. The fitness center was pretty decent for a small hotel. The staff was very helpful as well. I'm not sure if I would stay again unless I traveled with my mother and sister again and would need the 3 beds. I personally like to be right on the beach. If you use your hotel as a home base and hop around the island this is a great location though. There are several car rental locations on Seaside avenue and it is actually cheaper to just rent the car for the day street park it overnight (free from 6pm - 8 am) and return it in the morning rather than paying $20 a night to park. Overall, for the purpose of my trip this was a perfect location. If the noise wasn't an issue I really would not have any complaints at all. I should have mentioned the window in 604 to the staff but I was always running around and it kept slipping my mind.

There is a business center with printer so very convenient. I enjoyed my stay and will go back there again in my future visits.

<Author>Aerojeen
<Content>More Good than Bad When we booked this hotel, we weren't aware of its previous identity (The Coral Reef) where we had stayed once before - a huge mistake. We read the reviews of the Wave hotel post-renovation, and decided to take the chance. Our party of 4 adults have now just returned from a week-long stay at The Wave, and we must say, with a couple of exceptions, it was a nice experience.Upon check-in, they comp'd us an upgrade to our room from a 2-queen deluxe suite to their largest 3-queen Aloha suite (one bed in a separate area with a sliding door), which set a nice tone for our stay. The room was good-sized, with comfortable beds, nice flat-screen TVs and stylish furnishings. The bathroom, although small, worked, and was standardly outfitted. We immediately saw the need for additional towels, called housekeeping, and had our delivery within 10 minutes. All staff we dealt with were friendly and very willing to help in any way they could. They stored our luggage on two occasions, with absolutely no problems.So, here are the cons - not a long list, and most of which seem easily remedied by the hotel, which makes you wonder why they don't fix the ones they can (wouldn't you want better reviews?):1. LOCATION - this is a colorful and very loud part of town (nothing they can do about this), making parking questionable (although close and relatively convenient), and strolling the area pretty interesting. The after-hours activity made for some sleepless hours. 2. WINDOWS IN ROOM - as a result of #1, we noticed immediately that it seemed so loud in our 9th floor room that we assumed the windows/sliding doors were open. We confirmed on many occasions that they weren't. The window in the small room seemed especially poorly-insulated or installed. We were on the 9th floor, and it seemed like traffic and voices were directly outside our window.3. SLAMMING DOORS - our room was positioned at the end of a hallway, adjacent to the door to the stairwell. This door, which was frequently used, had no slowing mechanism on it, and slammed very loudly when shutting. We were awakenened out of a dead sleep many times every night as a result. This seems like such an easy fix...?4. BATHROOM FAN (or lack thereof) - as stated above, the bathroom was small, but for one person it worked fine...except that the steam from the shower had nowhere to go, so the room was steamy forever after a shower due to the absence of an exhaust fan. We were traveling with friends, making leaving the door open not so much of an option. Another easy fix...?5. PILLOWS - this could merely be personal taste, but as comfortable as the beds were, the pillows were just as uncomfortable. They were too firm and foamy for our taste. As we were checking out and awaiting our airport shuttle, we spoke with a lady who was on day 3 of her week-long stay at this hotel. She had the very same complaints we did, but also said that overall it was a good value at a decent hotel. We concur 100%. If you're looking for a beautiful view in a serene location, this is not it. However, if you travel like we do, and don't spend that much time in the hotel, this is a good value.Oh...I almost forgot...they do provide one set of earplugs in the room. We're certain they would bring additional sets for everyone. We would recommend this option if you're into sleeping.

<Content>Mixed Review We booked as part of a package with Hawaiian Airlines. Upon arrival to the hotel, they didn't have our reservation on file. We hit up their breakfast the next morning and it is pathetic. They had a tray of croissants, a tray of mini-muffins and a fruit bowl. Pretty lame, considering there are several restaurants in the area offering cheap breakfasts (probably to compete against lame hotel breakfasts that are free). My other major issue with this hotel is the pool. Even the bellman referred to it as their bathtub. There is no access from inside the hotel. It is accessed by going down into the parking garage and out the backside into an alley. The pool is up some stairs and fenced in chain-link with blue plastic privacy slats. It looks like someplace you'd find the dumpster and it butts up to the backside of the food court of the International Marketplace. I never saw anybody using it. The other main turn-off to this hotel is its location. It is not on the main strip - Kalakaua Blvd and it is not on the beach. We found ourselves walking at least quarter mile each way to the beach. We wasted so much time walking back and forth getting cleaned up for lunch, dinner, etc. It was a major pain in the [-].This hotel would be fine if you are in town on business or don't plan on partaking in any of Waikiki's attractions. But if you are looking for a Hawaiian experience, I would steer clear. If we go back to Waikiki, we'll be staying at the ResortQuest Waikiki Beach.

<Content>We Loved the Aqua Waikiki Wave We loved the Aqua Waikiki Wave! When we called into the reservations line for Aqua Hotels we were greeted with a very friendly and helpful agent. Yes you will hear the odd noise from other guests but nothing to complain about. The patio doors kept the noise from outside out of the room. The location is perfect! About 2-3 blocks from the beach. Very close to great shopping! A fave was Muse that had just opened 2 weeks ago and was directly accross the street. Upscale shops are along the beach. The International Market is literally next door to the hotel. The market has a food court and unique to Hawaii shops and kiosks. It, of course, has an ABC Store for convenience however you will find ABC Stores every half block in Waikiki!! (ABC Stores have everything you need as a traveller.) The hotel is located very close to many restaurants that have great deals for breakfast ($2.99 breakfasts to be exact for your simple eggs/toast/bacon etc). It's great for the budget traveller. There are many happy hour specials that serve $1.00 - $3.00 drinks! The hotel itself is great for all types of travellers. Great for families and singles / couples alike. The small pool is not in a good location however. It is accessed through the parkade and kind of in a back alley between 2 tall buildings - no sun. Very weird. The hotel might as well not have a pool at all really! :) HOWEVER this would be our only complaint and we didn't even want to swim in the pool anyway since you're in Hawaii for the ocean! The ocean swimming and waves are better by far. Towel service is offered at the front desk for the beach as a sign in / sign out. They were very nice about the fact that our towels were covered in sand and sea water! : ) Shuttle service to and from the airport is easy. $9.00 per person. or a taxi would be about $40.00 if you have a family for more than 3 people. We used Reliable Shuttle but there are many others with a simular price point.  Overall our stay was excellent! We recommend it to everyone!Any of the Aqua resorts seem great on their websites.

<Author>minnami
<Content>Not Bad At All We booked our stay from 3/17-3/23/2008. I travel a lot for work and am pretty picky about where I stay, but didn't really have any complaints. Please keep in mind that this is not a five star hotel that extremely pampers their guests (i.e. Ritz Carlton, Beverly Hills Hilton, Four Seasons, etc.), but a hotel that offers a little more than the basic for comfort at a reasonable price. We originally had booked with Hilton Hawaiian Village, as I am an HHonors Gold Member but felt that it was a bit too pricey (base rate of $270-$300) given the construction activity still in progress and distance from the more active Waikiki areas. After reading about Aqua Wave being newly renovated, cross-referencing reviews with other sources, and checking out the rates for our stay, we took the chance and changed from HHV to Aqua Wave. Plus we figured that we鈥檇 be out and about majority of the time anyway.I admit that we were a bit discouraged by the constant mention of street noise and *ladies* hanging around on the street in front of the hotel. But we booked rooms on the upper floors (15th floor) and didn't really hear anything that kept us from sleeping. I did see a few females on occasion outside the hotel, but they did not appear to be actively marketing themselves. For all I know they just could have been dressed to go clubbing given that they didn't dress too differently from the out-of-town girls who were ready to party. Actually, I had to point it out to my fiance who didn't even notice them.The hotel is close to everything and is on the same block as two ABC stores, Starbucks, and Jamba Juice. The room themselves are fairly big and they do look like the pictures. We had two queen (king?) beds, which were very comfortable, microwave, and mini-fridge. The bathroom is on the small side, but this is typically the norm with older hotels when compared to newer hotels across the US. The availability/speed of the elevators depends on the time of day. With only two elevators, you can expect a longer wait in the mornings, when everyone is leaving for the day's activities. Staff was nice, but didn't really rely on them so I can't say too much about them. The free breakfast is on the 1st floor, but we never tried it so I can't comment on that either. The parking lot is cramped and does get full in the evening/nights and costs about $18-$20. If it's full, they'll direct you to another parking company (cars parked by attendant via lift in various 'slots' located right before hotel's parking lot entrance) where the parking fee is waived. We found out that it's actually cheaper to just park it with them directly for $10 for over night parking (no in-and-out). We only have 2 minor complaints: (1) There is no ramp for rolling luggage. Although it鈥檚 not a long flight of stairs, we still had to lug our heavy suitcases up when we arrived and back down when we checked out. We did not look at all graceful doing this. But there is a lift to the side of the stairs for the handicap. (2) The hotel room doors do not have anything on the hinges to slow it down and stop it from slamming. We just had to catch the door to prevent it. So I guess the only noise complaint I have would be the slamming of doors when guests left early in the morning or got back late at night. But overall, we're happy with our decision to switch reservations and would book here again as long as the room and staff quality remains similar.

<Author>O'hAdoha
<Content>Great Hotel! We spent 3 nights at the Wave March 1st to 4th and came away very impressed. We are seasoned travellers and have stayed at many hotels around the world and can easily recommend the Wave. My only caution is that my Wife and I like smaller hotels and if you are looking for a mega resort on the water, this is not your place.The room was clean and well furnished. We had a Junior Suite on the 14th floor that had a King and a Queen bed with two balconies with a view of the ocean. Also, it had probably the greatest shower I have ever encountered in any hotel. (We stayed at a high priced resort on business on the big island right after this and the shower was not nearly as good) The staff was courteous and very friendly. They went out of their way to make our stay very pleasant.The hotel is in a great location in the middle of everything and a block and a half from the water. Ok now to the concerns others have laid out here:Noise: We realized that this was a big city location and a certain amount of noise comes with that. If you want silence you have to book a room in the country. That said, we slept with our windows open but had to close them at 4 am both Saturday and Sunday nights, the first for when the bars let out and the second night because of the garbage truck in the alley. This did not bother us at all. With the windows closed it was quiet and the hotel provided earplugs in our room if we needed more. We had friends who stayed at the Hilton Hawaiian Village on the water and had noise issues as well. They were not happy when they found out that we paid half of what they did and they had a view of a roof.Hookers: My radar may not be as well tuned as say an Elliot Spitzer, but we did not see any hookers. We were not out late on Saturday as it was our first night in and the nights we did come in late were Sunday and Monday nights.Tour operator: Did not use him. We did make one mistake. We took a cab to Pearl Harbor spending about $40 one way and then found that there is a van service that will pick you up and drop you off at your hotel for about $9 each way. Lesson learned.Pool: Did not use, the ocean is a block away!Overall our experience was very good and we would recommend it to our friends.One more tip. The Shereton has a bar on the water called Rum Fire. We watched the sunset from there every night. It has a great view and has fire pits and couches for a late night drink.

For the price I paid, it was well worth it.

<Author>RWLChan
<Content>Thumbs up! We are a family with three young children under the age of six. Our experience at the Waikiki Wave was positive right from the start. Yes, there was some noise, but one has to remember that the hotel is located in a desirable, heart of Waikiki area, so we knew this when booking the hotel. Downtown Chicago or any other big city would have citynoise also. Our children (6,4 and 1) had no difficulty sleeping (other than jet lag!) and neither did we. We'd recommend this hotel to others definitely, but for ourselves, may choose a hotel more off the beaten track, simply because we know we can walk to desirable areas within blocks. It was a wonderful location, however. Any drawbacks? Perhaps the stairs leading to the hotel lobby were a bit challenging, with a double stroller, but we managed. We booked a suite, which was great - due to the layout of the rooms, it was a little odd, in that, there were 2 queen beds in the living room. I know that they can't help this, but it would have been great to have two beds in the screened off portion and a couch/bed in the living room portion... a very minor detail. When we were leaving, thanks to Rachel, we were allowed to extend our room for 2 hours, to allow our babe to have a nap before leaving on an 8 hour plane ride. We SO appreciated her consideration!!! Overall, mahalo Waikiki Wave!

<Author>AndreToronto
<Content>Nice hotel You can spend weeks on the Internet looking at hotel reviews in Honolulu... there are 100's of hotels and reviews are subjective anyway. We've been in 100's of hotels in dozens of countries over the last 30 years and sometimes it astounds me what people's expectations are and what they complain about. If staying on the beach is your priority then expect to pay 3 times as much as the prices at the Wave.Overall, we had no problems and would definitely stay there again. It's a nice little hotel. You walk through the international marketplace across the main street and you can be sitting in front of the Royal Hawaiian.Our package included their $5 breakfast. It was not very good though. They provide only carbs, fruit and juice. No milk or protein. I had to bring my own milk. If it is in included, it's okay for a few days...but don't buy it as an extra. You can go get a $2.99 special down the street that is really good :-)The breakfast room is also very crowded; they could use a few more tables.Overall I would recommend this hotel to anyone and I will investigate it on our return trip to Oahu (which I hope is next year!).

<Author>estragon
<Content>OK for the price The positives: Good value - for $145 a night, it's not a bad place at all. Friendly staff - everyone was courteous and helpful. Decent-sized room, with a comfortable bed, smallish flat-screen TV, fridge, coffee maker, and good water pressure in the shower. A block and a bit from the beach. Close to cheap breakfast joints, Starbucks, etc.BUT.The parking garage is a joke. Small, with extremely tight spaces, and no self-serve elevator to the lobby. If you have a lot of stuff to transport (we were there for work and had equipment to bring up to one of our rooms every night), you have to call a bellman to come down and fetch you in the service elevator, which apparently is also used to transport garbage, or at least smells like it. Sorry guys, but this kind of garage just isn't worth $18, given that in other cities that kind of money gets you valet service and secure parking. Plus, if the garage is full (and it often is), you're out of luck -- have to park in one of the neighbouring garages for $25 a night.The bathroom lights were weirdly dim... and actually took a couple of minutes to warm up to something resembling full strength.There was a comfortable queen-size bed, but no night tables. One side had a small desk next to the bed, the other had nothing.Overall, the Aqua Hotels website presents the Wave as a funky, modern boutique hotel. In fact, it's nothing of the sort. It's a cheaply renovated tourist hotel that's OK for the price, but that's about it.TIPS:The Galaxy Steak House a few doors away is friendly and has a decent $3 breakfast, but it's dingy and dark. For a couple of bucks more, Keoni, a bit further down the road, has outdoor seating, table cloths, and great fresh fruit. It's also serves very good Thai food at night.Don't spend any more time at the Wave than you have to. Walk down to the beachfront Moana Surfrider -- the spectacular 100-year-old hotel on Kalakaua -- and hang out in one of the rocking chairs on the street side or deck chairs on the beach side. No one will bother you. Or go a bit further down to the Beach Bar and order an umbrella drink.

<Author>Rlove
<Content>It hit the spot! We stayed at the Aqua Waikiki Wave for 3 nights in December 2007, and had a good experience overall. We were on the 9th floor and had 2 double-beds in our room. The beds were comfortable, and the room was clean and had many amenities. The staff at the reception desk was friendly and helpful, as was the concierge staff (who helped us to rent a car for 1 day so we could explore the island of Oahu). The only drawback to this hotel is, yes, it is noisy (other reviews attest to this). I'm a fairly heavy sleeper and had a hard time due to the noise on my 1st night there. The level of street noise at this hotel's location is above average; I've stayed at hotels in midtown Manhattan that were quieter (the hotel does provide earplugs to help remedy this problem). There is an alley with small shopping vendors right next to the hotel (on the west side of the building, I think) where people pass through all day and night; a lot of noise comes from this area, even though the vendors close down at night. If you can deal with the noise, the Aqua Waikiki Wave is a great place to stay. It's clean, comfortable, and the location is perfect for exploring Waikiki and Honolulu.

<Author>RoamingSeattleite
<Content>Convenient, Good Value, Inadequate Housekeeping  I stayed at the Waikiki Wave for a week in early December with two friends.The hotel is a very good choice for decent accommodations close to thebeach and near lots of restaurants. The lobby could use a little updating to make the first impression more welcoming instead of a sea of hard beige surfaces with neon from the hotel signs and the Chinese restaurant in the lobby.The room was very spacious. We booked a Junior Suite Superior Wave, and each had our own queen bed, one of which was in a small bedroom separated from the main room by a sliding door. Aside from the beds, there was a shortage of actual chairs to sit on, except for two hard-backed chairs and the patio furniture. We all agreed that the beds were too soft.There were two small terraces, one facing towards the beach, which provided a view of other hotels, including the picturesque Royal Hawaiian and a tiny sliver of water. The other faced the parking garage of the neighboring office building and overlooked the market stalls lining Dukes Alley. Each had two white plastic lawn chairs.The bathroom really needed some work. It was impossible to get a hot shower and there was mildew in the shower enclosure. Also, the completely interior bathroom was dimly lit by compact fluorescents. This, according to one of my companions, made it really difficult to apply makeup.The housekeeping was really bad. I used one of the coffee mugs for orange juice and found it placed back by the coffee maker unwashed. Over the course of the week I tried various things that might get it changed - finally leaving it half-full of water worked! Most days, the beds weren't even properly re-made - the cover was simply pulled up and smoothed. Housekeeping also tended to ignore the do not disturbsign and knocked early in the day (before 9:30). On our last day, the housekeeper came barging in, claiming that she thought we had already checked out. (The door was unlatched because one of us went out for coffee.) Over the course of the week, we had to call the front desk for vital paper goods, as they had not been restocked. And finally, on the last day we discovered that our room door had been painted, as had all of the doors on our floor. Thankfully we were leaving as one of my friends is sensitive to paint fumes.The hotel pool was seriously disappointing. It's basically there so they can claim they have one. It's behind the hotel, accessible from an exterior stairway that you can reach only by waking through the underground garage and an alley and then climbing a flight of stairs up to the pool deck. It's surrounded by tall buildings and the back of the food court of the International Market, which gives off the aroma of fried foods. There's no way to actually use this pool and enjoy it or to sunbathe.Given that the hotel is a reasonable value, my friends and I rolled with the punches and enjoyed our trip. Even with the shortcomings I pointed out above, the combination of location and value would make me consider staying there again.

<Author>irun5k
<Content>Decent hotel- but reserve a high floor We stayed here for three nights. We are Hawaii residents so we got a discounted rate.The hotel is recently remodeled and is, in general, in good condition. However, an extra 20% effort in the rooms would have went a long way... for example replacing the old, dirty air vents or maybe some bathroom upgrades. Overall though, the room was clean and the bed slept well.This is not a resort, it is just a standard hotel, so you are basically paying for the room. The price includes easy, fast, free WiFi which is really nice considering the big resorts will really ding you for this.Many have said they had parking problems. We actually didn't go in and out a lot, but we never had issues parking. In fact, if you find a spot in their garage, it is really nice. This is the closest I've ever been able to park to my room in a Honolulu hotel. Perhaps, if you come back late you may have trouble getting a spot.Basically this is a good place to stay if you can get a good price and you don't need resort amenities. Don't underestimate some of the things the larger properties offer though. Even active folks who don't spend a lot of time in their rooms might enjoy being able to relax in the hot tub for a half hour under the stars at night in the warm tropical air. No can do this at the Wave.One other, MAJOR consideration. We were on the fourth floor and it was LOUD. I wouldn't stay here again if I couldn't get something on a high floor. Otherwise, check a property like the Ohana East and see if they have something on a high floor.

<Author>SeattleTraveller99
<Content>The Noisy Aqua Waikiki Wave! The one word I can use to describe the Aqua Waikiki Wave is.. NOISE! I booked a room at this hotel on the glowing reviews of the other travellers, and pre-paid for my entire week with my family. Had I not done this, I would have moved hotels after the first night. To be fair to the hotel, they are a great value in price for the location, but you end up paying for it in the noise. I'm not a light sleeper by any means, but I was travelling with my wife and 10 month old boy for our first vacation. He is a light sleeper. The room doors all seemed to slam shut, so at all hours our room seemed to shake whenever any of our neighbors shut their doors. Also, the walls seemed very thin as we could not only hear, but follow conversations our neighbors, or anyone in the hallway were having. This includes the shrill screaming of kids running up and down the hallway at all hours. We were on the 14th floor and I didn't think it possible that the noise from the street and bar down below would be so prevelant. Maybe it has something to do with the single paned glass balcony doors, they did not block out any outside noise at all. Our room was adjacent to the parking garage which operated constantly, adding to the orchestra of noises. It also appeared we were close to some sort of dumpster, because at about 3:00am every morning you could hear glass bottles? being dumped in large quantities. The hotel does supply earplugs, so it appears they know there is a noise issue. There was even one day that we had just gotten our little one down to sleep when the fire alarm went off! The staff came on the intercom and said there was no fire, however the damage had already been done. I ran into one of the maintenence guys and asked him what set the alarm off, he said it was dust in the fire alarm, and he had a can of compressed air in his hand as he had just come from cleaning it out.Besides the noise, there were other reasons we will not go back to this hotel. There is a small flight of steps going from the parking garage to the street, and then a larger flight going into the hotel lobby. There is no elevator. There IS an old wheelchair lift on the flight of stairs going to the lobby, however nobody ever offered to let us use it. So my wife and I had to carry our baby and stroller up and down these steps whenever we went anywhere, while the staff watched. I believe they offered to help once.Parking. With limited parking, if you did not get back to the hotel early in the evening, you did not get a spot. Now they would reimburse your $18 if you could not find parking, but the hassle was ridiculous. I rented a small SUV for travel around the island and found that even if there was a spot open, the vehicle could not fit into some of them because they were so small!Pool. In order to get to this tiny pool you had to walk through the parking garage, an up another flight of stairs at the back of the hotel. I never saw anyone there and we found out why. The pool was dirty. Bird feathers and dead insects floated across the surface. Completely unusable in my book.The saving grace for this hotel is it's price and location. It is minutes from Waikiki Beach and the International Marketplace. If I had known better I would not have booked at this hotel with our small child. Couples or families with older children may not find the challenges we had with this hotel.

<Author>SukhumvitRoad
<Content>Don't expect too much The reviews below are far, far too generous, apparently written mostly by people who don't stay at very many luxury hotels and therefore have limited expectations. This is not a good hotel. It is an okay hotel at best. Still, it is also true that Honolulu as a whole has fallen on bad times and there really aren't any good hotels in Honolulu any longer. Forget the glory days of glamour at the old Kahala Hilton. Honolulu hotels now cater to the Wal-Mart set, although you couldn't tell that from their ever-rising rates. All Honolulu hotels now are old, tired, and dowdy no matter what you pay.To be fair, this hotel may well be the best choice of a very modest lot, both in terms of quality and value, particularly the latter. I would certainly choose it over any of the alternatives of which I am aware, but I emphasize this warning if you follow my recommendation: don't expect too much. It's hardly anything you would call a good hotel by world standards.

<Author>permanantHoliday
<Content>Best Bet for the Money! The Aqua Wave is perfect for a homebase in Waikiki for the money.We loved how personally attentive and courteous the staff was, the super central location and simply but stylish updated room. Everything was right where we wanted it to be (shopping, beach, food, sightseeing) and the price couldn鈥檛 have been beat for this hotel. The A/C in the room was perfect and the lanai was a nice treat. The kitchenette (fridge/coffeemaker/microwave) was kept spotlessly clean and retained cold temperature for food and milk. Overall the room was clean, the beds so comfy (nicer quality linens too!). A continental breakfast (with a pass) next door at Big Kahuna鈥檚 was a typical fare of muffin/pastry choice with juice and coffee. Apples were also available. Complimentary hassle-free beach towels were available for outings to the beach. The Aqua Wave is a great choice for the casual traveler. A minor rebuttal to the concerns of illegal activity around this area--you are in a big metropolitan area. There will always be an element of watching for your safety. I can't believe how SAFE we DID feel here even with my daughters who are 8  10. Police presence was around constantly but not in a menacing fashion as in say LA or Chicago (and we did get a laugh at the officer dancing street while keeping an eye on the clubgoers). Honolulu is a major city. Keep your wits about you and all will be fine. Hawaii is home to more sincere humans than I think I've ever met! Aloha indeed! Relax-this isn't the Mainland is a good mindset to have. Things to keep in mind of the Aqua Wave if you are highly particular:Our room was decently sized but for 4 it was snug and we thought since there were restrictions on how many to book to a room, it would have been a bit bigger. We would stay at a sister property of the Aqua next time for a Jr. suite at a relative price.The bathrooms were not ample and could鈥檝e appreciated an upgrade to the tub to match with the whole room update. Since this is a hotel in the heart of the city, there is noise from the clubs and streets well into the AM. Not recommended for a sensitive sleeper (you do get complimentary earplugs however).but then again I can鈥檛 think of too many other places in the city that are for the quiet people. Parking is a premium at $18/day and the lot fills fast, however this is not unlike any other urban environment. Savvy parkers can seek offstreet spots nearby. There is no room service but several excellent choices of eateries within steps of the hotel. One small personal dislike--smoke could be smelled in the vents and I don鈥檛 know if it is because of intake sources but to the Wave鈥檚 credit, other nice hotels I鈥檝e been at have this problem too even when they are nonsmoking. I would absolutely stay with the hotel again as a first choice with a stay for two adults at the rates I had. For a larger group, I will be happy to try the other hotels in this chain when we come back! (PS-We were there when they were shooting photos for a brochure so whenever/wherever it is published, it is an accurate depiction of the hotel.)

All in all, this is a budget option, and it shows. I have rarely stayed in a louder hotel and one with stranger smells. As such, I don't recommend it. The only complaint, which we already knew about, was the noise in this area due to AM construction and garbage trucks. But this wasn't a hotel problem. One night, someone near the hotel was recycling glass bottles into a steel bin at 4:30 AM. This only happened once though. I think Wiakiki could really use a noise pollution plan, though. Anyone who's stayed in the heart of Wiakiki knows about the 6AM wakeup call from the garbage truck beepers, even if you're staying at an expensive beach hotelThe Wave had an interesting mix of people. This isn't a resort hotel, but who needs a big pool when the Pacific Ocean is a block and a half away. And the price is right.

<Content>Wow! This Hotel is Smashingly Superb! Our family of four from Penang, Malaysia stayed at Aqua Waikiki Wave for 4 nights (Aug 6th - 10th 2007) in our first-ever tour of the Hawaii and what a smashing experience it had turned out for us. It's a unanimous double-thumbs up from the 4 of us for Aqua Waikiki Wave (AWW) for living up beyond our expectations in its standard of value-added accommodation, front-office service and room service. We opted for the deluxe room on the 15th floor which offered a partial bluish seaview.Additionally, AWW is strategically and centrally located to most of the top-rated touristic must-sees and other coveniences: a. We did our whole-day Grand Circle Island Tour (not-to-be-missed itinerary for first-timers) and the pickup is just around-the-corner from the AWW; b. the bustling, colourful and bargainful International Market Place is just a few yards away and the stall owners are ever so professional, never scornful towards us for not completing any purchase; c. the world-famous Waikiki beach is just a few blocks away (we have the world-famous Batu Ferringhi beach at home but nothing beats the Waikiki Beach that is so FULL of people and activities. There is even a police beat base there to provide a great sense of security. On our second day of our visit to the beach, there was even a good samaritan standing near the beat base informing and cautioning us about the presence of jelly fish. Wow!)d. TheBus, a most convenient transportation in Oahu, has its stops just in front of and across from the AWW (We went to Chinatown and the very nice and upscale Ala Moana Shopping Center using this very affordable mode of transportation).e. A great bakery, St Germain, is just next door. (We ordered a wonderful birthday cake from them and was delivered to us on time.).f. The omnipresence of the ABC stores within Waikiki is greatly welcome and there's one with very friendly staff next to AWW. (We bought some of our souvenirs here as they are very reasonablly-priced.)g. AWW is also very near to reasonably-priced eateries. (We got to try the one at the corner of Seaside Av/Kuhio opposite the hotel for our breakfast for only $3 plus including coffee and the other one at less than $10 for all-you-can-eat buffet lunch on Kuhio opposite the AWW on the right.In summary and on behalf of my family, I would to thank Lynette, the GM of AWW, from the bottom of our hearts for making our check-in, accommodation and Aloha vacation so smooth, memorable and wonderful.Best regards, Patrick

<Author>flyingflyn
<Content>Aqua Wave Waikiki - great hotel We arrived at the Aqua Wave having travelled from San Francisco. The staff on the check in desk were very friendly and helpful. We had requested 4 rooms close together as we were two families travelling together with teenagers. We were allocated rooms on the 8th floor - all close together. The rooms had a small balcony but unfortunately this overlooked a carpark. However the rooms were spacious and comfortable and were equipped with tea/coffee making facilities and a fridge. The bathrooms too were good - and the showers excellent. The lifts/elevators in the hotel are very fast - which we appreciated!! The hotel is located a couple of blocks from the beach and a shortcut through the market makes the short walk very pleasant. The staff throughout the hotel were courteous and friendly. All in all - a very good hotel - not too far from the beach and within walking distance of many good restaurants, bars and shops. If you don't want to pay the high prices for a beach front hotel - then the Aqua Wave is an excellent option.

<Author>mbmpdx
<Content>Good value for Waikiki Stayed from Jul 19-23 in double room on 14th floor (with 2 balconies) and I have to say that for the money, the property is a good value for Waikiki. Almost next door to back-end of International Marketplace on Kuhio, and only a block to beach it is convenient to nearly everything. Hotel staff at front desk and housekeeper on our floor were extremely friendly, helpful and did their job very well. Room was very clean and modern (remod in last year or two?) -- with a somewhat smallish bathroom -- and other than the standard hotel door-slams in the hallways all hours, was fairly quiet and peaceful. I've taken ear plugs with me on trips for years as people just do not consider others with the doors in all but the finest properties that I've stayed at -- and with those, usually the doors are either very carefully padded and/or the closers dampened to prevent the jarring slams. If they were to address this issue, this property would be nearly perfect. Microwave, refrig and coffee maker in the room, with free safe (large enough for laptop, cameras, etc) and free WiFi are considerate value-added touches many places still feel the need to nickel and dime you to death with. Coffee replenished daily, though if you like more than a cup or two (it is 4 cup coffeemaker) you might want to bring 4 Cup Mr Coffee round filters with you as these are not supplied and a box of 100 costs about $3.50 at ABC store (we only stayed 4 nights, so that purchase wasted a lot of filters). A/C is central and kept the room quite comfortable, which is much better than window units that several economy properties have in Waikiki. There can be some hooker activity along a good stretch of Kuhio after hours (10 PM until 6AM) but certainly not a reason to discount the property, even if traveling with children.

<Author>kwai08
<Content>Great hotel, great location!!! We stayed at the Waikiki Wave from July 3-10, in a 1 bedroom room on the 6th floor and it was great !! For a second there I thought we had gotten a suite because I didn't expect the room to be so big for a 1 bedroom. Our view from our 2 balconies was of the parking lot across the street but we didn't care. The room had a big living room area with a fold out couch and a seperate bedroom area for the queen size bed. A Japanese style sliding door seperated the bedroom from the living room so this room could def sleep 3-4 comfortably. The room appeared to be remodeled because the furniture and fixtures were modern. The bathroom was a little tight but what hotel room bathrooms aren't right? The tub drained as it's supposed to, not like some of those other older hotel rooms where you're standing in 3 inches of water as you shower. The room and hotel was always kept clean. Fridge, microwave, free safe and wireless internet was great!! I suggest making a run to Walmart out there and stock up on water, drinks, snacks and microwaveable meals to save yourself some time and money when wanting a quick bite or drink. A good thing about the hotel was that it was secure. You needed your room key to enter the hotel from 10pm - 6am so only guests could gain access. The garage was a little tight and sort of small but we usually found a parking space. The hotel staff was very helpful and friendly. The hotel is located right behind the Beachcomber, next to and behind the Int Market Place on Kuhio Ave. There's a Jamba Juice, Starbucks and a Jack-in-the-box across the street. I've been to HI several times and this by far was the best hotel for the money I've ever stayed at. For about $110 a night, it might be a little more than other budget hotels but you'll be glad you stayed there. We will def stay at this hotel in the future!!

The beds are a dream and if I could buy one in Scotland I would have one the same in my home.Overall our stay was brilliant and we would definitely come back and stay in AWW despite the noise.Only negative comments were it was not much of a pool but we were informed that a new pool is on the cards which would be great for future visits.

<Author>toasty24
<Content>stay here only for value and location, not looks or luxury Let's face it: Hawaii is expensive. With all the major hotels being in the several hundred $$$ per night, Waikiki Wave is only slightly over $100. However, despite the boutique hotel logo and website appearance and a renovation (which i would just call slight remodeling), the rooms/facilities not cool or hip, and are nothing more than a 3 star standard---only it benefits from a great location (in the heart of Waikiki, you can't get better than this), and a smiling staff.The rooms are spacious (2 queen size beds) but the decor is pretty pathetic. maroon printed carpeting, furniture that shows wear, dark bathroom, etc. The room is clean enough, but not 5-star pristine. Bathroom has yellow lighting, is cramped, and feels claustrophobic. Mirrors have some fingerprints if you look carefully. The one bonus is that the linens are extremely clean and there is no gross puffy bedspread that you fear will never be washed---instead there is a waffle weave blanket sandwiched between 2 flat sheets --- brilliant. There is NOTHING romantic about this room. I would not recommend this for couples looking for a fantasy getaway b/c you will be disappointed upon seeing this room. Instead, splurge the extra $$$ and go to the Halekulani Hotel which is just breathtaking.I would recommend this place to groups of budget-conscious friends (not couples) looking for an inexpensive place to stay---a clean bed and a place to crash. You cannot beat this location as it is close to everything--as i said, it's in the heart of this area and everything is within walking distance--shops, the beach, other hotels, etc.No need to visit the pathetic pool which is *shudder* out by the parking garage. it is a sad, wading-pool-like small triangle of water that hasn't been skimmed in weeks. The gym was being renovated at the time so the staff gave me access to a 24-hour fitness (which faces Waikiki beach), only a 10 minute walk from the Waikiki Wave. Staff is typical Hawaiian, accommodating and nice, pretty good service, no attitude.If looking for a nice beach restaurant, i recommend the Hula Grill which is above Duke's Restaurant. This restaurant overlooks the beach from the 2nd floor and at night is quite romantic. PROS:-budget friendly-awesome location: close to beach, food, shops, etc.-clean beds and linens-nice staffCONS-rest of the room is um...motel-ish but not overly gross-not romantic for a vacation getaway-feels cheap

<Author>JO911
<Content>Great hotel for the price Stayed at the Waikiki Wave for 6 nights 5/28-6/3. This hotel is in a great location, a little over a block from Waikiki beach. I am not sure I would pay extra for the ocean view as there isn't really an unobstructed ocean view from here as there are other buildings just as tall if not taller in the way. We could see a small sliver of the ocean from our room on the top, 15th floor. We were on the street side and the noise on the street in the night was noticeable a time or two but nothing unbearable. The beds are really comfortable and the rooms are good size. I love that the beds are double sheeted and no nasty comforters touching any part of you! There is a bus stop right in front on Kuhio Ave. There is a coffe maker, fridge  microwave in the room which is a plus. There is also a Starbucks practically across the street and ABC stores on nearly every side within a block. The $3 off coupon at Da Big Kahuna for breakfast was a nice perk too, we ate there a couple of mornings. The local newspaper is brought to the doors of each room every morning. There was one night where there was a rowdy group in the hallway in the middle of the night but that's not really the hotels fault. The pool is teeny tiny and at the back of the parking garage so if you want a pool, go elsewhere. Who needs a pool when the beach is right there though? Beach towels are given out at the front desk. All of the staff we encountered was really friendly. I would definitely return to this property or recommend it to someone else.

<Author>xene
<Content>Wonderful Hotel in Waikiki If you are looking for the full resort experience with - lounging around a pool and waiters bringing you drinks with umbrellas while a Hawaiian band serenades you - this is not the place. If you want to spend $100s less, still be in the thick of things, and have a clean, comfortable place to stay, the Waikiki Wave is the hotel for you.We had a Deluxe Wave on the 9th floor facing the Waikiki Trade Center (Ewa direction). Others have complained about the noise, but I found it no noisier than staying in New York or San Francisco.The rooms are spacious and well appointed. What is advertised on their website is exactly what you get. The refrigerator and microwave are wonderful additions to any room for storing cold water and leftovers from our plate lunches and reheating them for a mid-day snack.It's true that this is an older, renovated property, but the only sign of this is in the hallways. But who really cares if you can see multiple layers of paint in the hallways??Free WI-FI is a bonus. I had problems loosing connectivity to the Internet (stayed connected to the WAP, but could not browse), filled out a comment card regarding this, and saw a technician reprogramming the WAPs the very next day. That's service.The only downside I found with the hotel was the parking situation. It's amazing to see how many SUVs and full-size cars try to park in spaces barely wide enough for a compact car. I actually watched a minivan attempting to pull into one of the spaces - it took 2 lookouts to direct the driver and 5 whole minutes before the feat was accomplished. Rather than using the parking below the hotel ($18/night with in/out privileges), we chose to use the public parking facility (attached to the Waikiki Town Center) located in alleyway leading to the hotel's parking. The bonus is that public parking is only $10/night (no in/out privileges) and the same exact facility is used by the hotel as overflow parking (at the $18/night charge). So do yourself a favor and park at the public lot. It's easier that way.Overall, I don't think you'll find another hotel that offers the friendly service and comfort for the price that you'll pay at the Wave. We'll definitely return again.

<Author>jesben79
<Content>Complete Review Hi, My family and I stayed at the Aqua Waikiki Wave from the 9th of May 2007 for 10 nights. Below I have posted a review in all areas I thought would be of interest to visitors.Location: The hotel is located right next to the International Market place. It is literally a 5-10 minute walk to Waikiki beach. Due to the location of the hotel, it does get quite noisy especially on Friday and Saturday nights, with music pumping well into the early hours of the moringing. This does get quite annoying, but is the whole city is busy so this hotel is not unique with noise. Reception: General Foyer area is OK. Nothing flash. There are toilets and phones located on the ground floor along with a concierge booking centre and 3 computers with internet access for $1 for 6 mins. The hotel has been refurbished. You can tell the hotel is ageing, but a good job has been done to refurbish and revitalise the foyer. The entrance to the hotel is accessible by having to walk up about 10 stairs. There is a lift the wheel chair access, but it was a bit of an inconvenience as we had 2 children and the use of a stroller was quite hard expecially with all the shopping / bag that we had. Rooms: Nicely renovated. We were in a partiual ocean view. To be honest, the view was crap. When the description is 'partial' it is very limited with how much ocean you actually see. It wasnt worth the extra cost for the ocean view. The balcony on the 11th floor did not lock, however when we requested a lock be placed on the door for the safety of the children, the maintenance man completed it straight away (very good). I would suggest that the hotel address this on all rooms and floors and parents need to know that the children cannot open the door themselves. The bathroom was clean with all amenties you would expect from 5 star hotels. The only thing I could say about it was that it is very very very small. Its alomost impossible giving 2 kids a bath without bumping into things.VERY COMFY BEDS.Pool: HAHAHA, dont waste your timeGym: DITTO . Breakfast (Aqua Start) This was a waste of time. Basically you get danish and juice from the restaurant next door or you can use the coupon to get $2 off any other menu item. Staff: Very nice. Always smiling, always willing to help. Would I stay there again? I would say no. Not because I didnt like the hotel , but because its the little things that you actually appreciate when on holidays.Eg: I didnt realise how much I missed laying in front of the pool, but the facilities at the hotel are like a old back yard swimming pool. The same goes for the gym. (But I understand the gym is being refurbished)It might sound pety to complaint about a hotel just because of the pool, but for me, going a holiday is about seeing the sights (including the beach) but also having the choice of just relaxing at the pool having a drink. Overall verdict: It is a very nice, clean hotel. Close to everything.Cheersbenjes (Aussie)

<Author>Jam18
<Content>Great Stay Enjoyed our stay with very few surprises thanks to all the Trip Advisor reviews posted. Arrived early afternoon and went directly to the hotel hoping for early check-in. Hotel signage was hard to spot, street in front of hotel had a small unloading area, so we turned down the side alley and parked underneath the hotel. We were able to check-in early, given 4th floor room facing parkade. Rooms were of adequate size, clean, beds were very comfortable. Rooms come with fridge/freezer,LCD TV, DVD player, microwave, hair blowdryer, coffee maker. Ice was available at the front desk, newspapers delivered to your door every morning. While we were there, they were painting the inside and exterior of the building, keeping everything looking fresh. After the first night, my wife asked the front desk to move us as the parkade creates a lot of noise- car hoist, cars lining up to park, people waiting for their cars. Without hesitation, they moved us to the 11th floor when a room became available - room was virtually the same except the view was of Waikiki downtown, and we were distant from the noise. The small pool is accessed by walking through the parkade to the back of the hotel, it is surrounded by solid fencing, has 8 lounge chairs, we didn't use it , beach was a better setting. Parking is $18 per day, underground holds only about 20 cars, the parking garage next door takes the hotel overflow. They have a business office, Internet available for a fee, and they also have at certain hours an activity desk to book your sightseeing trips or activities. This hotel is situated in a busy area, 2 clubs close by, the volume of people seemed to increased between Thursday and Saturday. Streetwalkers do walk Kuhio at night, along with touists and groups of people outside of the clubs, but we never felt threatened at all walking around at night. The hotel locks the doors at 10:00pm and you have to use your room key to enter the hotel. There is usually a doorman at front during the day and early evening, and a securtiy person during the late night. Hotel has a Chinese Restaurant inside, Da Big Kahuna Restaurant out front, St Germaines Bakery next door, and tons of other restaurants around - you name it, LL for plate lunches, Starbucks, Cheesecake Factory, California Pizza Kitchen, Sushi, Chili's, fast food, ramen houses, etc. For shopping, ABC stores (they're almost on every block)for snacks, drinks, sun tan lotion, beach mats, boogie boards, mac nuts, t-shirts, etc. There's a Food Pantry 1 1/2 blocks away for groceries and DVD rentals. The International MarketPlace for souveniers, and on the west side of the hotel, there are vendors with booths similar to the Int'l Marketplace. Behind the hotel on Kalakaua Avenue you'll find the higher end stores lining the street like Macy's, Coach, Nine West, etc. My wife found the jewellery stores, all of them.Closest beach access was 1 1/2 blocks away beside the Cheescake Factory on Kalakaua. Getting around on The Bus is $2 a trip, or you can purchase an unlimited 4 day pass at the ABC stores for $20. The maid service was very good, clean sheets and towels (they do not have a save the towel program) everyday, but the service and attitude from the front desk  doormen was the best. Always helpful and with a smile. We would not hesitate to return to this hotel.

<Author>1dolphindude
<Content>Great Place 4 a Great Price! I had read a few reviews about The Aqua Waikiki Wave complaining about the noise, the elevators,  the bathrooms. Well, you know what?
