However, the rooms are all done very nicely, very modern. My friend and I lucked out. We were given a corner room that was probably 1 1/2-2 times the size of a normal room. The bath room was quite small and needed some work but everything functioned. The elevators were alright. I've stayed at hotels where the elevators were MUCH slower. Unfortunately, one of the two elevators broke down while we were there and it was possibly at the worst time: the weekend. But it did get fixed come Monday and everything seemed fine. It could have been better if the pool were accessible from the hotel, instead of having to walk outside and around the hotel to get to the pool. But the beach is 2 blocks away. Why go to the pool? The hotel is, literally, right next to the International Market Place. Walk out the lobby doors, make 2 lefts. and you are at one end of the Marketplace. The staff were very friendly and eager to help give directions or whatever. The parking was a little difficult to find at first and it was first come, first serve in the hotel's parking garage. However, you could also park next door at the other garage so we never had issues with parking. Our room was on the 4th floor, facing Kuhio Ave so we got some of the noise at night. It seemed to bother my friend a bit but I slept through most of it. All in all, the hotel was great and I would definitely stay at the Aqua Waikiki Wave again.

<Author>Tren2414
<Content>Despite some reviews - this hotel was awesome! First off - I went to tripadvisor.com to see what hotels I wanted to stay in. I then looked at websites for some good deals. This allowed me to not have to pay in full like the other website! When we arrived the hotel entrance was very appealing. I stayed on the 8th floor and they rooms looked just like the photos on their website. The bathroom was nice with the marble counters and amenties! I'm thinking the people who where complaining of the noise must have had a hangover since the noise wasn't that loud. People in Hawaii don't honk their horns as often as other states! The staff was very friendly even dealing with a couple of my family members that can be very demanding and loud (then being from NYC). When I ask for something to be sent to my room, it was promply delivered! The Bellboy was nice as well and very happy for a tip for our luggage. He acted as though it was his job to help us with our luggage rather then it was our duty to give him a tip for carrying our luggage. They also have a concierge desk which was helpful and it was either the same price as what you would pay for your own for your daily excusion or cheaper! The beach was only a 3 minute walk and EVERYTHING you needed was in walking distance. Overall this hotel is great and a bargin because of location,service and the room. If I would compare this hotel to a popular chain, it would be the Marriott. I would come back time and time again!!!

<Content>Worth a look We stayed at the Waikiki Wave from Jan 11-Jan 18. They fixed the water pressure while we were there. It is now quite the shower! The front lobby was very clean  our rooms were cleaned well each night. We did tip the housekeeping staff every morning and also wrote a note regarding what we needed in our room like extra towels, coffee, etc. - that may help. Our sheets seemed to be changed enough - I don't change my sheets at home nightly, so if they went 2 days in between it was OK with me. The staff was generally nice and helpful - we do have a problem with our charges, though, as we were charged for parking every day  only used the parking garage 2 days. It is $15/day to park, however this is very standard at ANY hotel you choose to stay at in Waikiki. There aren't very many parking spaces - there are more than 10, though, and we found a spot to park easily both nights we had a car. The hotel was a trick to find! watch for the Big Kahuna restaurant, or the Saint Germains bakery which are very close by. We drove past it 3 times before figuring out that you turned in directly beside the hotel and drive down an alley to park.

<Author>SaskatchewanCanada
<Content>okay for price Hello from Canada! I love the Trip Advisor Review Site and find it very beneficial when booking a hotel. Traveler鈥檚 comments have helped us many times when deciding to stay at a hotel. So here are my experiences and I hope it helps you when you book your stay in fantastic Waikiki!!We stayed at the Aqua Waikiki Wave from Dec 24/06-Jan 7/07. We stayed at the hotel when it was called the Aston Coral Reef about 5 years ago and it was nasty. Big improvement since then. Although, I found it was a quick fix renovation. My question is why would you spend 7.5 million on a renovation and not upgrade the shower/bath system?!? The shower SUCKED! You couldn't even get the sand off your body. You got more pressure from the tap in the sink!! Our toilet also got plugged but the maintenance man was fairly quick to repair it. The hotel carpet looks like it was a cheap quality as it was already worn and torn in the elevator. I realize that this is a highly used area, however the reno's were just done in October and it's only January. Can't imagine what they will look like in a year or more!Don't be fooled by the photos on their website (no flowers or silk plants). Nor do the beds have the nice white cover that they show on their website. It's just a white sheet (which is fine by me as I assume they wash them along with the rest of the bedding?!?). Speaking of washing, during our 2 week stay our sheets were only changed twice. Sometimes the maids didn't leave us any towels so we had to call down for them, but they were prompt. For the most part, the maids were pretty efficient and nothing was stolen like other hotel quests. As per other readers comments regarding noise, you're going to get noise anywhere in Waikiki. It's a hoppin' city!! Don't let that discourage you. You are definitely wise to stay on the east side of the hotel as the parking lot on the west side isn't the most beautiful view! We asked to be moved because of that reason along with the fact that we had mold on our tiles in the shower. Something you don't expect after reading a relaxing place of escape that is cleverly hip on their website. Mold is not cleverly hip in any shower folks!! Another frustration that we had (especially myself as I am a contact lense wearer) is the fact that all the towels were brand new and you ended up being covered from head to toe with lint. Even the beach towels (which are nice and big) were lint distributors. So maybe by the time you visit they will all be broken in and lint free! You could not get any radio stations on the clock radio provided, so if you like music or like to be woken to music, bring your own!The front desk staff were okay. I found Trevor to be the nicest. The rest just seemed like you were an interruption to their day. Some days they had candles burning in the lobby which was a very nice touch (and aroma) and sometimes they had apples in a basket which was also a nice touch.When checking in we never received our coupon book, continental breakfast coupons or free beach bag coupon. When we asked for them it was no problem. The continental breakfast (which was posted on the website as delivered to your room daily when we booked our stay) was not the case (I see they've changed that now). You had to go to the Big Kahuna outside of the hotel and it was a joke. The danish was the size of a cracker and the coffee was a small cup - no refills. We used it one day and never went back. If you want a great breakfast go the Shorbird Restaurant in the Outrigger Reef on the Beach Hotel - fantastic!!!Overall, for the money (we paid $128 a night) for a Superior Wave room, the hotel is okay. The best part of the hotel is the location as you are close to everything. For the most part you are not in your room, so it is an affordable, clean and bug free place to stay.There is a lot of construction going on in Waikiki and eventually it will be a new little city. As for other other hotels to stay in, check out Embassy Suites Waikiki Beach Walk - a little pricier but it's a top notch place and it's brand new....top to bottom. I'm sure it has great shower pressure too!Best of luck during your stay in beautiful Waikiki....wherever it may be!

<Content>Great experience My wife, my daughter (10 yrs) and I stayed at Aqua Waikiki Wave (AWW) between 12/19 and 12/26 with the average cost of $130/day booked from [--]. We like this hotel very much. It's located in the center of the Waikiki area, one block from the beach. The famous International Market Place is at the next door. It's one short block from the Kalakaua St. which has many restaurants and brand-name shops. The hotels on this street cost at least 30% more than AWW. The Seaside Gill Bar which serves good breakfast with the lowest price in town is one block away. The Check-in process was fast. The hotel employees are friendly. One time I asked a location which was not on a map, an employee printed a Mapquest direction for me. They provided beach towels for free. There is an Expedia.com desk in the lobby. We bought tickets for Ploynesian Culture Center from the agent. We also got an Expedia shopping bag from her. It's a free gift even people do not buy anything from her. We stayed in the 12th floor. The room is more 300 square feet with partial ocean view. The room is very clean with microwave, refridgerator, a flat panel TV and a DVD player. The newspapers are delivered at the door each morning. The hotel gives us 14 $3 cupons which can be used for breakfast in a restaurant next door. Parking is crowded. In two nights, we came back late and had to use the overflow parking facility, which is next to the hotel. It is not convinent to get our stuff after our car is stored. Parking fee is $15/night which is common and relatively cheap in the Waikiki area. The hotel restaurant serves Chinese food. Food quantity is small and the quality is so so. In general, we like its location, roomy and clean room and friendly and helpful employees.

He told me how to get around the town (without a rent car), the best restaurants, places to visit, tours available and he would get you a taxi in no time. She was out helping hotel guests, assisting the check in folks, and passing on parking and local information. She was doing this each day! Talk about special attention to guests. The hotel is on Kuhio Ave, less than a block from the international Marketplace. There are several shopping areas close by, we had a several choices of places to eat within easy walking distance. There is an 鈥淎BC鈥?and 7-11 stores (convenient stores) within two minutes walking distance from the hotel, to pick up some snacks and those small forgotten items. Waikiki beach is an easy 10 minute stroll from the hotel. With many small shops and stores along the route, we passed on getting a rental car. The only down side to the trip to Hawaii, was being there during the earthquake! Well talk about a hotel stepping up and taking care of their guests. Electricity was lost for the entire island after the earthquake for over 10 hours. Lynette McDonald (general manager for the hotel) was all over the place assisting and calming nerves. I asked her about how she was handling all this, she had never been thru an earthquake and here she was taking care of all us and reassuring us. The hotel鈥檚 generator had the lobby area functioning and well lit, so well many people off the street wanted to come in thinking this hotel was the only one in the city with electricity. The hotel staff and hotel Owner (yes, the Owner showed up), provided food, soda, water, fans, and earthquake information all day. When we go back to Hawaii, we will stay at this hotel. Our stay was almost like staying with friends you have known for awhile. The front desk, maids, and James (don鈥檛 know his title), and everyone at the hotel has a help the guest anyway possible attitude. Great place to stay, great value. Even on checking out, the front desk folks printed my boarding pass for my flight back. We are already thinking about what to do on our next visit to Hawaii, we know what hotel to stay in.

<Author>Michie-G
<Content>Needs improvement I stayed at the Wave for a week at the end of October. The rooms looked great - everything was new and there was even a flat screen TV. I had no problems with the fittings or furniture, but what I did have a problem with was the bathroom - it was tiny, and you could tell the shower/bath was still from the old hotel - which I did not like. The shower pressure sucked too, a normal 10-minute shower ended up taking half an hour because the water came out in a weak stream. And the water in my sink took ages to go down --- about an hour. That was not good. I also didn't like the bed linen - the sheets and blankets were thin and pilled. Definitely not the high quality kind you'd expect from a boutique hotel. I also had problems with my door as it did not close properly. You had to literally slam it shut. I was not happy with the housekeeping department. Not once during my whole week's stay was my coffee decanter washed or even rinsed! I found the cleaning staff to be very shoddy with their job. It seemed like they were just intent on getting in there, doing whatever they could in a few minutes, and getting the heck outta there without making sure they had done their job properly. Does anyone even check if the staff have cleaned the rooms properly? Also, they didn't bother making my beds right. I came back one afternoon to find my sheets neatened out on the bed but not tucked in. On the positive side the Wave is in a great location, and the front desk staff are friendly and helpful. You can still see traces of the Coral Reef at the Wave, but I suppose with time, that will go. If the Wave wants to be considered a boutique hotel by well-travelled customers like myself, they need to lift their game by investing in better quality bedlinen, hiring more competent and energetic cleaning staff, and seeing to their plumbing and water pressure problems. Otherwise I thought everything else was OK.

<Author>bashfulLV
<Content>Had a great visit! I booked a package to Hawaii through an online travel agency/website and was booked into what was then the Coral Reef Hotel on Kuhio in Waikiki. I had stayed at the Coral Reef in the past - due to the area it is located in (right behind the Int'l Market Place) I knew it would be okay even though I was well aware that the Coral Reef had seen better days. I was just thrilled to be going to Waikiki!A couple of weeks before the trip I wanted to look up something in the hotel ammenities list and could not locate Coral Reef online at all. I knew they'd recently been purchased by the Aqua Resorts group, so I went to their website, located the address on Kuhio and found it now belongs to the Waikiki Wave. I then discovered that the renovations had just been finished and they were having their grand re-opening with the new name - Waikiki Wave.The renovations included the entire hotel and took a run-down, tired hotel and made a little gem of it. The front desk/lobby area is the nicest part of the project - IMHO. The hallways are freshly painted with new carpet - but it wasn't a really great job, but I'm quite a nit-picker (I watch too much HGTV!), but it is better than it used to be. The elevators could have used some updating, though, but you can't have everything. I never went to the pool so I can't comment on that.The rooms were newly painted, but (like the hallways) it was over the previous paint, which is obvious in some spots (like a few places where it is already peeling off), but it looks better and is cleaner than it was before. Overall the renovated rooms are nicer than they were, but there was a lot left lacking for a renovation project of such a magnitude.The showers still have the original old tiles and hardware - faucets and showerheads are very outdated, but the marble vanity top and sink are nice, as are the matching marble tops in the bedroom. While taking a bubble bath one evening I noticed the old pipes underneath the bathroom sink/vanity area and it was apparent all they'd done in this area was slap on some paint - and did a pretty sloppy job of it too. The bathroom door had been previously damaged - you could see the ripples of it through the new paint job - the bottom of the door was jagged and the paint was already peeling off; they had put shiny new doorknobs on though. One thing that I thought was pretty disgusting were the vents - they had been painted over but you could see how terribly dirty they were - they obviously never cleaned them before they painted them. What it boiled down to (IMO) is that the renovation of the rooms themselves consisted largely of many cans of paint and hanging up some pretty pictures. They did upgrade the frig and add a microwave which is great. The complimentary newspaper each day was a plus I enjoyed.Although I did find some things to complain about, on the whole I enjoyed my stay and the new hotel and would stay there again in a heartbeat. The staff was friendly and helpful. The location can't be beat. I loved sitting on the lanai and watching the birds and the shoppers down on Duke's Lane and looking out over the top of the Royal Hawaiian. The parking situation needs some tweaking but the staff indicated that was in the works. I would not hesitate to recommend this hotel to anyone who is budget-conscious, but not to those who want a lot of perks and luxuries - this just isn't the place. But if you want an affordable, safe, decent place to lay your head, store your stuff and shower off while you're in Waikiki - this is a great place.
